  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_05792a84-f526-48e5-af3a-6d414ce3e9c7'

<span id="freeTextContainer12006403770736435668"><b>The Barnes & Noble Review</b><br/>Fans of Tamora Pierce's stellar saga about Alanna of Trebond can now get all four books one boxed set!<p><br/><br/>Packaged together for the first time, the Song of the Lioness quartet is the adventurous story of one girl's journey to overcome the obstacles facing her, become a valiant knight, and save Tortall from conquest. Alanna douses her female identity to</p></span>
  <span id="freeText12006403770736435668" style="display:none"><b>The Barnes &amp; Noble Review</b><br />Fans of Tamora Pierce's stellar saga about Alanna of Trebond can now get all four books one boxed set!<p><br /><br />Packaged together for the first time, the Song of the Lioness quartet is the adventurous story of one girl's journey to overcome the obstacles facing her, become a valiant knight, and save Tortall from conquest. Alanna douses her female identity to begin her training in <i>Alanna: The First Adventure,</i> and when she gains squire status in <i>In the Hand of the Goddess,</i> her growing abilities make her a few friends -- and many enemies. Books 3 and 4 complete Alanna's adventure and secure her legend, with the new knight errant taking on desert tribesmen in <i>The Woman Who Rides like a Man</i> and seeking out the powerful Dominion Jewel in <i>Lioness Rampant.</i></p><p><br /><br />A must-read for Pierce's loyal followers and a perfect starting point for readers not yet familiar with her work, this boxed set is fantasy writing at its best. Pierce's gifted writing -- and her knack for creating heroines unafraid to challenge the status quo -- shines brightly in this Lioness set, taking it to the highest ranks, just like Alanna herself. <i>Shana Taylor</i></p></span>
  <a data-text-id="12006403770736435668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/112378433-ellie">Ellie</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">TLDR; Yes. I would let my 10 year old read these books. <br/><br/>I was 10 and in grade 6 when I read these books. Unless a child has been sheltered from life, <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">TLDR; Yes. I would let my 10 year old read these books. <br /><br />I was 10 and in grade 6 when I read these books. Unless a child has been sheltered from life, if they like adventures, they'll likely love the book. <br /><br />The "sex" mentioned below is not a deterrent and there are absolutely no details. They didn't make me "grow up" earlier, however they did influence my strong mentality of fighting for the things I want.<br />I've loved them so much that I've re-read them as an adult and I can't wait to, eventually, have my kid read them. :) Only as an adult had I realized how these books were amazing for creating such a strong female character lead. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_337716332" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/337716332" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9813065-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589145593p2/9813065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/337716332?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/9813065-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9813065-cheryl?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer337716332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15319141875792773617">At the risk of sounding TOO enthusiastic, this series changed my life. The heroine, Alanna, is one of my favorite characters, from any book. Alanna is a girl who wants to become a knight, except that girls aren't allowed. So she disguises herself as a boy and sets out to become one anyway. Alanna is an incredible character. When I was younger, I basically wanted to be her when I grew up. She's stubborn, determined, and incredibly brave, but also human--she makes mistakes, she has struggles, and </span>
  <span id="freeText15319141875792773617" style="display:none">At the risk of sounding TOO enthusiastic, this series changed my life. The heroine, Alanna, is one of my favorite characters, from any book. Alanna is a girl who wants to become a knight, except that girls aren't allowed. So she disguises herself as a boy and sets out to become one anyway. Alanna is an incredible character. When I was younger, I basically wanted to be her when I grew up. She's stubborn, determined, and incredibly brave, but also human--she makes mistakes, she has struggles, and she's not always sure of herself.<br /><br />The series has a host of memorable characters, with new ones arriving in later books as well. A couple of favorites include Prince Jonathan, every girl's dream of a handsome and charming prince, and George Cooper, the roguish and equally charming King of Thieves.<br /><br />They all live in a world of swordplay and tournaments that is nevertheless grounded and believable--swing a sword around too long and you'll have sore muscles. They also live in a world of magic. Alanna possesses the Gift, which she can use for various spells, some practical and some dramatic. There is also an entire pantheon of gods who occasionally step into mortal affairs.<br /><br />The books are funny, exciting, engaging...amazing.<br /><br />And they changed my life. I'm a firm believer that a girl can do anything a boy can do, that women have the same rights as men, and that we all ought to be equal, whether in pay rates or in who cleans the house. I'm sure a lot of that belief comes from my parents, especially my mom, but I think reading about Alanna at a young age helped!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15319141875792773617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1138383384" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1138383384" />
    <a title="Debbie Zapata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22110057-debbie-zapata"><img alt="Debbie Zapata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451631863p2/22110057.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1138383384?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie Zapata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie Zapata" href="/user/show/22110057-debbie-zapata">Debbie Zapata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780739431047" href="/book/show/153809.Song_of_the_Lioness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22110057-debbie-zapata?shelf=saturdaymx">saturdaymx</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138383384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16482568755247311961">This four-in-one volume book contains Tamora Pierce's books featuring Alanna of Torbald, a girl who dreams of becoming a knight. She sets out at a young age to meet her destiny, disguising herself as a boy in order to learn how to live the life she knows she is meant to live, and eventually lives proudly and confidently as a lady knight.<br/><br/>Alanna's story is fast-moving, exciting, and well-told. One reason I don't like to read many books in a series format is that there are always pages or even chap</span>
  <span id="freeText16482568755247311961" style="display:none">This four-in-one volume book contains Tamora Pierce's books featuring Alanna of Torbald, a girl who dreams of becoming a knight. She sets out at a young age to meet her destiny, disguising herself as a boy in order to learn how to live the life she knows she is meant to live, and eventually lives proudly and confidently as a lady knight.<br /><br />Alanna's story is fast-moving, exciting, and well-told. One reason I don't like to read many books in a series format is that there are always pages or even chapters needed to re-tell in subsequent books what happened in earlier ones. But here Ms. Pierce manages to weave necessary information into the stories without creating that 'Time Out While We Flashback' feeling that can be so annoying. <br /><br />I think Alanna is a good example of a role model for girls who need to be able to believe in themselves, even when they know they are different from everyone around them. It is not always easy to live your own life, follow your own guiding star. The temptation to follow the herd, to be a sheep, is strong. But it is infinitely more rewarding to discover our own inner Lioness, to become who we are meant to be. This is what Alanna learned. I hope all young women can learn the same thing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16482568755247311961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129772339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer842734546088224453">One day, while working at my middle school library, I stumbled across the first of this series. The fact that the girl/boy on the cover had a purple glow around her fascinated me, so I picked it up, judged it by it's cover (I was still doing that back then) and started reading. <br/><br/>Then I picked up books 2-4 and took them all home the next day. And zoomed through them! I couldn't believe it... this was the most amazing series I had ever read! Knights, and disguises, and coming of age, and magic and </span>
  <span id="freeText842734546088224453" style="display:none">One day, while working at my middle school library, I stumbled across the first of this series. The fact that the girl/boy on the cover had a purple glow around her fascinated me, so I picked it up, judged it by it's cover (I was still doing that back then) and started reading. <br /><br />Then I picked up books 2-4 and took them all home the next day. And zoomed through them! I couldn't believe it... this was the most amazing series I had ever read! Knights, and disguises, and coming of age, and magic and romance, all in one! It was a magical world for me to escape into. And I think I'm still stuck there, 7 years later! <br /><br />These days, this is my least favorite series of the Tortall books. Well, it sort of ties with Kel's series. There is just something slightly boring about knights for me now. I think I prefer magic (and justice?) in the long run! (Go Beka!!)<br /><br />Of the four books, The Woman Who Rides Like A Man was my favorite, and still is. In the Hand of the Goodess is my second favorite. I love reading Alanna: First Adventure because of her disguise and all the tricks she pulls on that rude boy. But the last book? Yeah, don't like it too much. (Some how I had the same order with The Immortals quartet!) <br /><br />I reread these books from time to time, and probably will for the rest of my life. I don't care that they are YA, they don't feel YA for me (except that they are over too soon!) Pierce has a great writing style, that just gets more refined with the years (see Beka Cooper's series!) </span>
  <a data-text-id="842734546088224453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2443850652" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2443850652" />
    <a title="Narrative Muse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/83302298-narrative-muse"><img alt="Narrative Muse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529545759p2/83302298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2443850652?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Narrative Muse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Narrative Muse" href="/user/show/83302298-narrative-muse">Narrative Muse</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2443850652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17089947432915202970">– Enjoying Song of the Lioness for ten years and counting –<br/><br/>Tamora Pierce was recommended to my sister. She devoured all of Ms Pierce’s books and I, as a dutiful younger sister, quickly followed suit.<br/><br/>I love Pierce’s characters, especially those in The Song of the Lioness series. Every year I reread the series, and even after a decade, I love the books as much as I ever did.<br/><br/>I want to spend my special reading time with the characters of The Song of the Lioness quartet. I want to talk to them after </span>
  <span id="freeText17089947432915202970" style="display:none">– Enjoying Song of the Lioness for ten years and counting –<br /><br />Tamora Pierce was recommended to my sister. She devoured all of Ms Pierce’s books and I, as a dutiful younger sister, quickly followed suit.<br /><br />I love Pierce’s characters, especially those in The Song of the Lioness series. Every year I reread the series, and even after a decade, I love the books as much as I ever did.<br /><br />I want to spend my special reading time with the characters of The Song of the Lioness quartet. I want to talk to them after reading a particularly bad book or when I’m in a reading slump. Yes, I realize they’re characters in a story, but the magic lies in the fact that they feel so real to me.<br /><br />The series starts with Alanna: The First Adventure. Alanna, a plucky young ten-year-old, and her twin brother are unhappy with their lot in life. Alanna comes up with a plan: they’ll pretend that they’re twin boys.<br /><br />Alanna disguises herself as a first born son and heads to the palace in the capital city to train to be a knight. Meanwhile, her brother goes undisguised to the cloisters to learn to be a mage.<br /><br />Alanna: The First Adventure is a story of a girl ready to fight for what she believes in. It’s a story about growing up and deciding who you want to be.<br /><br />I love Alanna’s courage and her enviable fortitude in the face of horrible situations. She lets nothing stop her, even though she has to learn how to be a knight as well as learn how to be a boy.<br /><br />While book one covers Alanna’s years as a page, the sequel, In the Hand of the Goddess, covers the remaining years of her training. The Woman Who Rides Like a Man and Lioness Rampant make up the rest of the series. <br /><br />The friends (and enemies) Alanna makes on her journey are amazing, sly and utterly believable as people. They have real quirks, real flaws. The dialogue reads so easily it’s like being in their company rather than reading them in words.<br /><br />Reading these at age twelve was a completely different experience to reading them in my twenties now. When I was twelve, I related to what happened to Alanna. I didn’t disguise myself as a boy, but I did go through puberty and first crushes and body image issues. But, with her by my side, these issues were a little easier. I looked up to Alanna. She was who I wanted to be: fearless, kind, hard-working and she’s a redhead!<br /><br />Now, as an adult, I read the series for the great relationships and friendships. I’m drawn to the way Alanna behaves around others, protecting her secret as well as standing up for her friends. I like the way that she turns down suitors in order to look after herself first, even though it hurts. And of course I also like the love story.<br /><br />I still look up to her, but for a whole new set of reasons.<br /><br />This series is one for young girls (or boys, for that matter) entering their teens to read. And for those who read it back then, I suggest reading it again. You may be like me, and find new meaning in the story on the pages in front of you.<br /><br />This review was first published on Narrative Muse, <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://narrativemuse.co/books/song-of-the-lioness">http://narrativemuse.co/books/song-of...</a>, and was written by Maiko Lenting. Narrative Muse curates the best books and movies by and about women and non-binary folk on our website <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://narrativemuse.co">http://narrativemuse.co</a> and our social media channels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17089947432915202970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2694281385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2694281385" />
    <a title="Rajkumar Pagey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21981319-rajkumar-pagey"><img alt="Rajkumar Pagey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373191187p2/21981319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2694281385?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rajkumar Pagey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rajkumar Pagey" href="/user/show/21981319-rajkumar-pagey">Rajkumar Pagey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781481416498" href="/book/show/20759527-the-song-of-the-lioness-quartet">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21981319-rajkumar-pagey?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21981319-rajkumar-pagey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2694281385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9548334023657394595">All Alanna of Terbond wanted to be was a Knight. Or so I thought.<br/><br/>1. Alanna: ★★★★★<br/>2. In the Hand of the Goddess: ★★★★<br/>3. The Woman Who Rides Like a Man: ★★★<br/>4. Lioness Rampant: ★★<br/><br/>I absolutely fell in love with the first book of the series. <br/>After that, it slowly became a chore.<br/><br/>It is a good series. Just not one for me.<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1374403820" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1374403820" />
    <a title="Kelsey Brennan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2346170-kelsey-brennan"><img alt="Kelsey Brennan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577481623p2/2346170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1374403820?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelsey Brennan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelsey Brennan" href="/user/show/2346170-kelsey-brennan">Kelsey Brennan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1374403820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2121318748237242604"><i>The Song of the Lioness quartet is the adventurous story of one girl's journey to overcome the obstacles facing her, become a valiant knight, and save Tortall from conquest. Alanna douses her female identity to begin her training in <b>Alanna: The First Adventure</b>, and when she gains squire status in <b>In the Hand of the Goddess</b>, her growing abilities make her a few friends -- and many enemies. Books 3 and 4 complete Alanna's adventure and secure her legend, with the new knight errant taking on desert</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2121318748237242604" style="display:none"><i>The Song of the Lioness quartet is the adventurous story of one girl's journey to overcome the obstacles facing her, become a valiant knight, and save Tortall from conquest. Alanna douses her female identity to begin her training in <b>Alanna: The First Adventure</b>, and when she gains squire status in <b>In the Hand of the Goddess</b>, her growing abilities make her a few friends -- and many enemies. Books 3 and 4 complete Alanna's adventure and secure her legend, with the new knight errant taking on desert tribesmen in <b>The Woman Who Rides like a Man</b> and seeking out the powerful Dominion Jewel in <b>Lioness Rampant</b>.</i><br /><br />I was first introduced to Tamora Pierce’s Tortall with The Immortals series when I was thirteen. After devouring those books, I backtracked and read Alanna’s story, already knowing how it ended. That didn’t make it any less marvelous, and I’ve since re-read all of the Tortall books many times. Each time, I find something new to love, and each time, I particularly relate to a different main character. In the past, Alanna was never a character I particularly related to, and I wouldn’t have counted her series as my favourite. This time, though, I was shocked by how emotional I got upon reaching the end of <i>Lioness Rampant</i>. I was fully invested in these characters; in Alanna, Jon, George, Thom, Thayet, Coram and the rest. <br /><br />Of all the Tortall series, Alanna’s is perhaps the most expansive. We not only get to see Alanna grow from a child to a woman, and from a page to a knight, but Alanna also grows substantially emotionally. Watching her relationships develop, whether they are friendships, romances, familial relationships, or enmities, shows a real breadth of human experience, right alongside an exciting tale of combat and sorcery. We learn, alongside Alanna, that there is no need to choose between the two, that both can exist at the same time. <br /><br />Regarding her romantic relationships, I think that Pierce promoted some genuinely realistic and healthy relationships. There was emotional conflict within all of them, and frank discussions and ruminations on whether or not characters were willing to accept the negative elements of their partners alongside the positive. Particularly groundbreaking for a young adult series, Pierce acknowledges that sometimes loving someone is not enough to keep a relationship going, and ending relationships can be natural, and though it is painful, you can move on. Too many novels, for both youth and adults, romanticize the idea of true love, but maintaining relationships is hard work, and even if you love someone, that doesn’t mean you want the same things out of life. <br /><br />It’s also worth noting that Alanna works hard for everything in her life, not just her romantic relationships. Alanna’s knight training teaches the lesson that you need to work to achieve your dreams, and that just because something doesn’t come easily to you, doesn’t mean it’s not worth doing. Alanna’s skills as a swordsman are not innate, they were hard fought for and earned. <br /><br />Of course, not everything about the series is perfect. Although I enjoyed seeing the portrayal of different cultural groups when Alanna was with the Bazhir, that storyline did seem to invoke the trope of the <i>white saviour</i>. Alanna is the catalyst for all sorts of “revolutionary” change among the Bazhir, and although she is the main character, the implications of having a white character as the instrument of social development among a non-white group portrayed as more "savage" than the white culture is somewhat problematic. <br /><br />However, that doesn’t stop me from recommending this series as a starting off point into the wonderful world of Tortall whenever I’m asked for a middle school recommendation. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2121318748237242604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer716598541255502514"><i>Alanna: The First Adventure</i> is the perfect book for the young teen girl. Seeing as I’m nearing my mid-twenties (no more teen demographic, sigh), my opinion might be a bit harsher.<br/><br/>The story is fast-paced, full of magic and knights, handsome men, thieves and animals. The female protagonist, Alanna, is —well, close to perfect: chosen by the gods, magical, pretty, martially talented, smart, stubborn, loyal and kind. The bad guy is easily predicted and the love interests also cornered down quickly. <br/>I</span>
  <span id="freeText716598541255502514" style="display:none"><i>Alanna: The First Adventure</i> is the perfect book for the young teen girl. Seeing as I’m nearing my mid-twenties (no more teen demographic, sigh), my opinion might be a bit harsher.<br><br>The story is fast-paced, full of magic and knights, handsome men, thieves and animals. The female protagonist, Alanna, is —well, close to perfect: chosen by the gods, magical, pretty, martially talented, smart, stubborn, loyal and kind. The bad guy is easily predicted and the love interests also cornered down quickly. <br>I don’t like overly perfect personalities, since they’re a fraud, but in this story, I don’t mind. It’s meant to be easily digestible and a fun read, which it is. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397817774ra/9332044.gif" width="400" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The end was weirdly rushed, and I thought it was a mistake when the novel ended. “Hmm, is this edition faulty?” But apparently, no.<br><br>This book is like a bag of candy, you know it won’t really help your fat percentage (intellect), but it’s oh so nice to chew on for a while. And psst, you just ignore the cavities breeding in your brain.<br><br>2.5-3 star rating. Right now I’m feeling thirteen again, I will be reading the next instalment. <br><br>Review of book two.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Alanna's definitely a bit emotionally confused in this book. Whoa! A 2.5-3 star rating. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Review of book three.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1397929744ra/9347845.gif" width="350" height="175" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What the heck is up with Jonathan? When did he change to dick-mode?<br><br>Some people disagree, but I liked the way Alanna acts in <i>The Woman Who Rides Like a Man</i>. A pretty mature woman, who knows herself well, even if she's unsure of what she wants in the end. It really messes me up, every time she feels alienated. Other than that, the plot felt a bit loose. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[But really, I'll hate this series if she ends up with that spoiled brat, Jonathan. Gods.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>2.5 stars. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Review of book four.<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The fourth and last instalment of <i>Song of the Lioness</i> was something of a clusterfuck. <div id="review_2202382369" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2202382369" />
    <a title="Allyce Cameron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14786420-allyce-cameron"><img alt="Allyce Cameron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402314705p2/14786420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2202382369?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allyce Cameron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allyce Cameron" href="/user/show/14786420-allyce-cameron">Allyce Cameron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2202382369" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11907003609521331866">I’m sure I sound like so many other reviewers of this series but these books <i>changed my life</i>. Tamora Pierce is the reason I started reading fantasy, and probably the reason I read so much now. Twelve year old me just loved the idea that girls can be whatever they want to be and don’t have to let men dictate how to behave. Thinking now it’s probably when feminist me was born as well. <br/><br/>Reading this as an adult is very different. I can clearly see now that this was written for younger teens and it s</span>
  <span id="freeText11907003609521331866" style="display:none">I’m sure I sound like so many other reviewers of this series but these books <i>changed my life</i>. Tamora Pierce is the reason I started reading fantasy, and probably the reason I read so much now. Twelve year old me just loved the idea that girls can be whatever they want to be and don’t have to let men dictate how to behave. Thinking now it’s probably when feminist me was born as well. <br /><br />Reading this as an adult is very different. I can clearly see now that this was written for younger teens and it shows. To be honest I think the reason I still love it now is only because I read it in my peak formative years, and the characters are so deeply embedded in my soul. Rereading this was like meeting old friends again after a long time. Alanna, George, Jonathan, Raoul, Gary and Myles to name a few. Every time someone came in I was getting so emotional! I don’t know that adult readers who have never read it before would enjoy it, it’s a little choppy and the characterisation isn’t amazing. But it’s definitely an amazing series for 10-14 year olds who are just starting on their reading journeys. Love love love!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11907003609521331866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_161019801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/161019801?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candi Criddle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candi Criddle" href="/user/show/882173-candi-criddle">Candi Criddle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/882173-candi-criddle?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161019801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12292338484129104563">I read these books when I was a kid, or at least the first two because that was all the library had. Cross-dressing to become a knight, boyfriends, horses, it was about all my 11 year old self could handle. I checked them out over and over thinking they were pretty risque, (she mentions her <i>period</i>). I wanted to read them again to see if they were as good as I remember, and to find out the end of the story that I have hung onto for 20 years.<br/>The answer is yes and no. They aren't quite as thick and</span>
  <span id="freeText12292338484129104563" style="display:none">I read these books when I was a kid, or at least the first two because that was all the library had. Cross-dressing to become a knight, boyfriends, horses, it was about all my 11 year old self could handle. I checked them out over and over thinking they were pretty risque, (she mentions her <i>period</i>). I wanted to read them again to see if they were as good as I remember, and to find out the end of the story that I have hung onto for 20 years.<br />The answer is yes and no. They aren't quite as thick and thought out as the books for kids these days, plus the heroine has purple eyes. And they aren't even that romantic, the raciest line is "his arm snaked around her" woo. But, when your other option is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77767.Little_House_on_the_Prairie__Little_House___2_" title="Little House on the Prairie (Little House, #2) by Laura Ingalls Wilder" rel="nofollow noopener">Little House on the Prairie</a>, they are not too bad. I'm proud of my young self for liking a heroine who dates around instead of finding her soul mate at the age of 16. Also the story <i>is</i> about a girl, not a boy, and a girl who goes out and fights for her life instead of whatever it is girls do in novels.<br />So, I had decent taste for an 11 year old and I would put this on the shelf for the next 11 year old to find.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12292338484129104563" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_162565508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162565508" />
    <a title="Devin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5299285-devin"><img alt="Devin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534979657p2/5299285.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162565508?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Devin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Devin" href="/user/show/5299285-devin">Devin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162565508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16891460050198968424">These books (along with the Wild Magic series) were and are my favorite comfort books. Alanna is an incredible heroine! She is brave, strong, perseveres, and isn't perfect (gasp!). She's short, stocky and has a wicked temper. I love imperfect heroines, not just ones that think they are. She owns her sexuality as well and is never ever painted in a negative light because of it. In a male-dominated society, she succeeds because of her grit and determination. I reread these books every couple of mo</span>
  <span id="freeText16891460050198968424" style="display:none">These books (along with the Wild Magic series) were and are my favorite comfort books. Alanna is an incredible heroine! She is brave, strong, perseveres, and isn't perfect (gasp!). She's short, stocky and has a wicked temper. I love imperfect heroines, not just ones that think they are. She owns her sexuality as well and is never ever painted in a negative light because of it. In a male-dominated society, she succeeds because of her grit and determination. I reread these books every couple of months. They aren't the most complex books, but the stories and characters are wonderful. Tamora Pierce has created a fascinating society and expands upon it in future novels as well.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16891460050198968424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6499332-jessica-rossana-sawin?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6499332-jessica-rossana-sawin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6499332-jessica-rossana-sawin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217075366" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3981959084221802944">The first time I read this series, I was twelve years old. Now, years later, they still remain among my all-time favorite and I re-read them every chance I get (at least once a year). These books are for the dreamers who believe in magic and in the power of their dreams. It is a wonderful coming-of-age story and resonates not just with young girls but the young at heart as well. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3338709718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3338709718" />
    <a title="Lynsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75893073-lynsey"><img alt="Lynsey" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3338709718?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynsey" href="/user/show/75893073-lynsey">Lynsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3338709718&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3338709718" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8744395793557807679">I think this series should get 3*s from me, even though I can't deny the eagerness and 4* reaction I had reading the ending, I had problems with unearned love for Alanna, the abrupt resolutions (though tha may be as I love slow burners) and the that everyone seemed to know and share everything which is unrealistic for people and kingdoms. The three men falling loyally in love with Alanna and doing everything for her was unrealistic, though it didn't give me YA hives (these books are not YA). Mag</span>
  <span id="freeText8744395793557807679" style="display:none">I think this series should get 3*s from me, even though I can't deny the eagerness and 4* reaction I had reading the ending, I had problems with unearned love for Alanna, the abrupt resolutions (though tha may be as I love slow burners) and the that everyone seemed to know and share everything which is unrealistic for people and kingdoms. The three men falling loyally in love with Alanna and doing everything for her was unrealistic, though it didn't give me YA hives (these books are not YA). Magic seemed a bit ruleless and classically Alanna was gifted without putting any effort in which is annoying. My other biggest problem is that things weren't addressed, aspects that should have been and would of been heavily considered by real person, like Alanna and Thoms relationship and the changes they go through, and the impact Roberts betrayl would have on Jon are just bypassed. I felt it was a shame. I feel like I've slated these books but there was so much to love also. I love Alanna traing to be a knight. I loved her dedication. I loved that she was good because she earnt it. I loved her and Jon's relationship founded on respect not attraction. I loved her friends she met as a page. I loved how hard se worked trainging. I loved the suspision of Robert. I loved the war in book 2. I loved the frenxy and drama of the ending. I loved that Jon married a Queen. I love that Alaan was strong and honest and a little niave but never blind. I love that she achieved so much. I love that she struggled. I loved Liam's ending even though it hurt. I loved George's honour. I loved so much about these books.<br /><br />Book 1= 4*s, thought it was great, loved the whole knight training, loved the mutal respect Alanna earnt from her fellow knights, though their is the classic issue most books have where the main character earns the love attention and loyalty of multiple influencial people and they don't all ring true. For example George - why the hell would the King of the Rougues care so much and trust this random boy and then let him tell his secret to all her friends. My main real issue was that the ending was rather abrupt and easy. They just went to the black city and did some undoable feat with ni build up. I don't beilve it. Alanna never earnt or learnt the magic she used in that senario and the easy victory and sudden worship by the bazhir felt rushed and weird. Overall though, still love this book.<br /><br />Book 2 = 4*s but again the ending was abrupt, the battel with Roger seemed to come from nowhere and I think her reveal as a women could have been more profound. I loved the whole war bit, though the romance between Jon and Alanna was a little YA for me during the kidnapping. Also I feel Thom and Alannas relationship would be very heavy and it wasn't addressed at all.<br /><br />Book 3 = 1* Nothing happens in this book. It is so boring. The beginning is highly unrealistic - shes just magically accepted and respected by a Bazhir tribe and manages to change thousands of years of tradition just by being there. It all seems a bit ridiculous. Jon and Alaana also annoy me in this. The whole plot for John to be the voice is just as crazy as alanna being beloved by the tribe. I found the shamon story boring, though in the latter books I see its purpose as realigning Alanna's relationship with magic. The visit to George - I blive george loves her, I don't belive her feelings for him enough. They seem kind of fartherly. Speaking of dads - we conveniently forget all about Alanna's real dad. There is no way he would just never be mentioned again or that he was so ubothered by his kids that he didn't get wind of Alnna or that she would be so unbothered by his lack of attention. Finally the vist o the sorceress to get the envelope (map) was just shoved in unelegently to serve the next book. <br /><br />Book 4 = 4.5*s so I think this book was alright until the end which had me entranced. The beginning - the quest seemed silly, Liam's intrest seemed just a author saying 'well we need a love interest', though I do like hs character. This books a bit of an everyone loves Alanna fest for my taste. I also hated how everyone knew who she was and worshiped at her feet when they were in a different bloddy knigdom. Also, Alnna just seems to spill entire plots and secrest randomly to everyone - that doesn't ring true. It would be idiotic for a confidont of the king/prince to blurt out this stuff to people at the first meeting. The quest in the montain again was resolved in a couple of hours of hiking and a god that just kind of went yeah, have the magic jem I sent storms to protect, no biggie. But once everyone was back in the capital and the story got going I was hooked. All those elements I didn't like were still there but I could stop reading, desperate to watch this story resolve. Bits were confusing, like the Alanna's gift giving to Jon, but overall I had come to loe and care for all these character and suppored their plight. The final was dramatic and finally the author gave an ending the pages it required to tell properly. I will admit I never really belived in the final romance of George and Alanna, but I did believe the moving on of Jon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8744395793557807679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1841668012" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1841668012" />
    <a title="Jemma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4705713-jemma"><img alt="Jemma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591960760p2/4705713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1841668012?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jemma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jemma" href="/user/show/4705713-jemma">Jemma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780739431047" href="/book/show/153809.Song_of_the_Lioness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4705713-jemma?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4705713-jemma?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1841668012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer500096000424206729">This book holds all four novels in the series of the same name: 'Alanna: The First Adventure', 'In the Hand of the Goddess', 'The Woman Who Rides Like a Man', and 'Lioness Rampant'. So that I didn’t get saturated by over-exposure to this world created by Tamora Pierce, I spaced out the individual books so that I finished one in December 2017, one in March 2018, one in May 2018 and the last at the end of July 2018. This was enough time in between each book for a break whilst still being able to r</span>
  <span id="freeText500096000424206729" style="display:none">This book holds all four novels in the series of the same name: 'Alanna: The First Adventure', 'In the Hand of the Goddess', 'The Woman Who Rides Like a Man', and 'Lioness Rampant'. So that I didn’t get saturated by over-exposure to this world created by Tamora Pierce, I spaced out the individual books so that I finished one in December 2017, one in March 2018, one in May 2018 and the last at the end of July 2018. This was enough time in between each book for a break whilst still being able to remember the story well enough for the next instalment. <br /><br />As a note, this quartet is followed by several further series in the world of Tortall, and most recently a new series started in 2018. I feel that having a longer break between series is OK because they will follow new characters and storylines! I’m also very excited that there is such a wealth of further books in this universe for me to get into in the future.<br /><br />Onto the book.<br /><br />When we get to know our protagonist in the first book, we meet Alanna of Trebond. She is of a noble family but her father does not seem very interested in his children, Alanna and her twin brother Thom. When their father tells them that Thom will go to the palace to become a knight and Alanna will go to the convent to become a lady, Alanna hatches a plan. Thom is not interested in being a knight and Alanna refuses to go to the convent. Under their distracted father’s nose they swap places, Thom going to the convent to study magic and Alanna going to the palace. With the help of faithful friends Alanna passes as a boy, “Alan”, in order to fulfil her dreams of becoming a knight.<br /><br />The setting of these stories is quite medieval. These books are about honour and victory, achievement and courage, and looking out for your friends and family even if that family is adopted.<br /><br />The first novel is about Alanna’s struggles of blending in as “Alan” in a patriarchal world. As the novels move on, we see Alanna grow up somewhat and we get to know her friends and see her develop meaningful relationships, albeit as “Alan”. She also gets her own cat companion with whom she can talk and he warns her of coming danger. This made me very happy! There are threats at Court where people fall ill and the royal family are in danger. **Spoiler alert!** Alanna becomes a knight. :) She can then go adventuring and makes a name for herself.<br /><br />Throughout the novels there are various romances with different men in Alanna’s life (after they either find out she is a woman or she has announced it). I liked how she was not a lovesick young woman pining over one man and wondering whether he likes her, obsessing. She was very down to earth and practical. She made sensible decisions, such as deciding when a romance had run its course, and I found her very relatable. <br /><br />Overall, a spectacular series and I will not hesitate in picking up the next series after a little break.</span>
  <a data-text-id="500096000424206729" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2455845611" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2455845611" />
    <a title="Ragon Duffy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50869751-ragon-duffy"><img alt="Ragon Duffy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451600768p2/50869751.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2455845611?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ragon Duffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ragon Duffy" href="/user/show/50869751-ragon-duffy">Ragon Duffy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2455845611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer160391055448799725">I'm going to count these as a single book instead of the 4 separate books they are for simplicity's sake and because I read them as a whole, not individually. <br/><br/>The summer I was 9 I check out Alanna from the library every week and read it obsessively over the summer. While I always enjoyed fantasy books as a kid like the Hobbit this was the first fantasy book I loved deeply. Finally one that centered a girl doing amazing, heroic stuff and used her grit and determination to succeed in a world that </span>
  <span id="freeText160391055448799725" style="display:none">I'm going to count these as a single book instead of the 4 separate books they are for simplicity's sake and because I read them as a whole, not individually. <br /><br />The summer I was 9 I check out Alanna from the library every week and read it obsessively over the summer. While I always enjoyed fantasy books as a kid like the Hobbit this was the first fantasy book I loved deeply. Finally one that centered a girl doing amazing, heroic stuff and used her grit and determination to succeed in a world that didn't believe women could do that. Upon re-reading, I can see how much Pierce's writing has grown and how being allowed to write longer books later on (she has said that the success of HP showed the YA/middle grade publishers that kids would read longer books so she took advantage of that in more recent years). I don't know if Alanna has quite the depths of characterization as Keladry or Beka and I think that Tortall is more fleshed out in future books. But I still found the whole series enrapturing and charming. <br /><br />Maybe knowing more about Tortall now, I wished for more details, even more world building. And I found things that were glossed over or plot holes that could have been filled. (Seriously, what was Alex's motivation, really?? If Roger's motivation in the last book was destruction, why was Alex signing on to that? WTF? That bothered me). And some of her gender politics read today, and even in comparison to her more recent books, still have a bit of retrograde tinge. More than one male character kisses Alanna despite her protests and she likes it. I didn't notice it at the time and it wasn't uncommon certainly in the early 80's as a relationship trope. But I thought it a bit jarring considering Alanna as a whole. But even as a kid the fact that Alanna was an equal in desiring sexual pleasure was sort of revolutionary.<br /><br />Still, it's a favorite for a reason and it will probably always have a place close to my heart. And I'm delighted how Alanna lay the ground work for so much more in Pierce's later work. Alanna is the hero of my childhood and she's still a worthy one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="160391055448799725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2086040550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2086040550" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2086040550?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/69218544-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69218544-sam?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69218544-sam?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2086040550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13829728270165850936">I'm trying to work out why I haven't enjoyed this too much. It's not that I am just reading it as an adult and therefore outside the target audience - I'd read one of the Circle books as a child, and none of the Immortals books, and I quite enjoyed both series (although I doubt I'll reread them now).<br/><br/>I've re-read Protector of the Small over and over again since I was a child, that being the only series I possessed of Pierce's. While I read books one and two of the Lioness from the library, I didn</span>
  <span id="freeText13829728270165850936" style="display:none">I'm trying to work out why I haven't enjoyed this too much. It's not that I am just reading it as an adult and therefore outside the target audience - I'd read one of the Circle books as a child, and none of the Immortals books, and I quite enjoyed both series (although I doubt I'll reread them now).<br /><br />I've re-read Protector of the Small over and over again since I was a child, that being the only series I possessed of Pierce's. While I read books one and two of the Lioness from the library, I didn't finish the series because I didn't have the other books.<br /><br />I think there's two main things at play. For me, I didn't like Alanna. It's hard not to compare her with Kel, and in contrast Alanna (and Jonathan, mind) come across as being very petulant and self-centred. I suppose that's what you'd need for the 'first girl' - someone who doesn't care about what she asks of others (bullying Coram for example to get them to swap) but still it doesn't sit right. Kel also just seems to knuckle down and work hard where Alanna complains and whines through most of the series. Second, I feel the characters are much more flat and one-dimensional than in Pierce's later works. Apart from George, who at least has a bit of a spark, all the other characters are disappointingly bland. <br /><br />Look, it was fine. But for an author that I otherwise love, that's damning with faint praise.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1869180474895636926">I actually read The Imortalls and went back and read everything in order when I was a teen. I would recommend reading them in the correct order... <br/>I have owned three different editions of this series... my first i wore through the spines. The second I found the original printed copies at a thrift store, I LOVE the original artwork. They’re in better condition. This edition I love that it is all in one book, although it’s getting to be a little battered because I read it almost every year. <br/>For an</span>
  <span id="freeText1869180474895636926" style="display:none">I actually read The Imortalls and went back and read everything in order when I was a teen. I would recommend reading them in the correct order... <br />I have owned three different editions of this series... my first i wore through the spines. The second I found the original printed copies at a thrift store, I LOVE the original artwork. They’re in better condition. This edition I love that it is all in one book, although it’s getting to be a little battered because I read it almost every year. <br />For an adult, you may not like the writing style. It may be a bit simple. For a YA reader, you will love it. Either way the story itself is fantastic. Tamora Pierce really builds an entire world you can disappear into. <br />Alanna really inspired me as a teen. When I joined the military and went through basic training I thought of her struggles and used her as an inspiration to keep myself going. In Afghanistan I thought of her determination, stubbornness, and perseverance to see things through, then embodied that in myself. <br />I recommend this book to every early reader, especially young girls, because it really had such a huge impact on my life and I hope it can inspire others as well. I also recommend the entire realm of Tortall to anyone who wants to immerse themselves in a world of adventure and fantasy. Happy reading!</span>

<div id="review_2692358167" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2692358167" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780739431047" href="/book/show/153809.Song_of_the_Lioness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30079754-octavia-cade?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30079754-octavia-cade?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2692358167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10392154804316918572">I actually read and reviewed all volumes in this collection separately, so this is basically just a note for my own records. The three star rating is an average of what I gave the individual entries, all of which were three star reads themselves apart from <i>The Woman Who Rides Like A Man</i>, which only got two due to sudden and inconsistent characterisation of two of the supporting characters, who turn into jerks for no reason. On the whole, though, it's an enjoyable enough series, and the real stre</span>
  <span id="freeText10392154804316918572" style="display:none">I actually read and reviewed all volumes in this collection separately, so this is basically just a note for my own records. The three star rating is an average of what I gave the individual entries, all of which were three star reads themselves apart from <i>The Woman Who Rides Like A Man</i>, which only got two due to sudden and inconsistent characterisation of two of the supporting characters, who turn into jerks for no reason. On the whole, though, it's an enjoyable enough series, and the real strength of it lies in the main character. Alanna really is likeable - kind and brave and hardworking - and she bypasses the "not like other girls" trope by valuing typically feminine things as well as her role as a warrior, because she's perfectly capable of appreciating a pretty dress <i>and</i> being good with a sword. On the other hand, her accumulation of incredible talents becomes ever more unbelievable, and there's an irritating love triangle which lasts until the final book, where yet another love interest is added (love quadrilateral?). No matter how many people were involved, I didn't like it, anyway. I swear, love polygons of any description are the scourge of YA. Would love to read a series without one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10392154804316918572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2822899237" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2822899237" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23017567-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2822899237?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/23017567-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780439968218" href="/book/show/153801.Song_of_the_Lioness_Quartet">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2822899237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15975523271759967787">I read the first three of these books when I was young and adored them. Alanna was my hero.<br/>However, I never got my hands on the fourth book - until now! I saw this compilation in a charity shop and decided I should really find out what happened to Alanna after all this time. <br/><br/>I was a bit worried that they wouldn't stand up to re-reading after all this time, but they absolutely did. I still really enjoyed all the stories and adventures, not to mention the characters - who are heroic, but also flaw</span>
  <span id="freeText15975523271759967787" style="display:none">I read the first three of these books when I was young and adored them. Alanna was my hero.<br />However, I never got my hands on the fourth book - until now! I saw this compilation in a charity shop and decided I should really find out what happened to Alanna after all this time. <br /><br />I was a bit worried that they wouldn't stand up to re-reading after all this time, but they absolutely did. I still really enjoyed all the stories and adventures, not to mention the characters - who are heroic, but also flawed. I like the messages that come across through the books - that you don't have to be naturally talented to become talented if you work hard, the importance of friendship and love, and that women are just as capable as men.<br /><br />I'll admit that 5th star is probably heavily tinged by nostalgia - there are parts of the books that don't quite flow as nicely, or, in the case of some plotlines in the 4th book, even really make sense.<br />However, I thoroughly enjoyed revisiting this world and am now considering checking out some of the sequels. Not bad for a book series I first picked up 20+ years ago!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15975523271759967787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/101956512-elizabeth?shelf=novels-lit2019">novels-lit2019</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3133071920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9107181590953332512">(For my Novels and Literature Class: multiple books by the same author)<br/><br/>Ever since I received this box set for Christmas one year, this has been one of my favorite book series, which lead me to explore some of Tamora Pierce’s other books and loving those too. I love the magic system and wonderful characters she creates in her Tortall universe, and I can’t seem to get enough of Alanna and her knightly shenanigans and adventures. The theme of accepting yourself is prevalent throughout, as Alanna ev</span>
  <span id="freeText9107181590953332512" style="display:none">(For my Novels and Literature Class: multiple books by the same author)<br /><br />Ever since I received this box set for Christmas one year, this has been one of my favorite book series, which lead me to explore some of Tamora Pierce’s other books and loving those too. I love the magic system and wonderful characters she creates in her Tortall universe, and I can’t seem to get enough of Alanna and her knightly shenanigans and adventures. The theme of accepting yourself is prevalent throughout, as Alanna eventually reveals she is a girl and, later on, accepts her Gift. It could be considered more middle-grade than YA, but the themes of romance, (at least in the beginning books) being a teenager, and having difficult relationships with a parent or peers are still there for people to relate to. I could go on for hours, but I will end it here. It’s a wonderful world in the realm of Tortall, indeed.</span>

<div id="review_3178979184" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3178979184" />
    <a title="Pippa Hoover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/109758352-pippa-hoover"><img alt="Pippa Hoover" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581014091p2/109758352.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3178979184?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pippa Hoover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pippa Hoover" href="/user/show/109758352-pippa-hoover">Pippa Hoover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/109758352-pippa-hoover?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/109758352-pippa-hoover?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3178979184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8143378596091672514">I love this series and probably always will. I grew up with mild dyslexia, and struggled to read anything until I found these books around 11 or 12. For the first time, I'd found a story that was fun and exciting enough to make me push past my reading difficulties. I love Alanna as a protagonist: she's tough, fiery, and determined not to be constrained by her gender role. But she's also flawed, vulnerable, and works hard for everything she achieves. The other characters are great, too (especiall</span>
  <span id="freeText8143378596091672514" style="display:none">I love this series and probably always will. I grew up with mild dyslexia, and struggled to read anything until I found these books around 11 or 12. For the first time, I'd found a story that was fun and exciting enough to make me push past my reading difficulties. I love Alanna as a protagonist: she's tough, fiery, and determined not to be constrained by her gender role. But she's also flawed, vulnerable, and works hard for everything she achieves. The other characters are great, too (especially George!), and there's a great deal of focus on Alanna's friendships, not just her romances. The Song of the Lioness quartet is not without flaws, the most glaring being some white savior narratives that are pretty cringy, and my ratings for individual books in the series are lower to reflect that. Also, the villains were a little one-dimensional and the plots are pretty predictable. Still, I've lost count of how many times I've read The Song of the Lioness quartet, and it reigned as my favorite book series for many years in my adolescence. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8143378596091672514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZcZlrIIXJHj1Cxnl/j4a4LSTmoMcBCvJ3fL4psB+D/ECTAkYChe3eLx/ShnmoaWTb/TRYR7zplUOKma89N9mDQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('O3vVgRwz2yIsmKNQDAxEzS5UX5Ye14xaV+k24iIvJKNc8bk1lDNIImXs8KwUk/u+9TMUdBwgAcaEMaj4Fo5NXw==')})
  }
//]]>
